I can't tell, but the wood you used from your yard looks like pine. Pine is toxic to most reptiles. So is cedar. You should also be mindful of any pesticides used on trees and plants. Lizards, like the frilled dragon, look and act like LIZARDS. Not dinosaurs.

Fun fact: dinosaurs dont look like a lizard wit ha frill on it, nor do they act like one. the real dinosaurs are birds. Birds belong to the theropod group of dinosaurs that included T. rex. Theropods are all bipedal and some of them share more bird-like features than others. Archaeopteryx, discovered in 1861, was for a long time the only truly bird-like dinosaur â€“ it's from the Late Jurassic era (150 million years ago). To spice it up when you get a REAL dinosaur, try to get a ratite like a cassowary or Emu. sure it doesn't look like a dinosaur, but it is a dinosaur.

Cool animal, few things to note though, frilled dragons often get put in too high of humidity, the Australian ones live in arid areas and tropical grasslands and scrubland, never let humidity exceed 75% for Australian frilled dragons(50-70% is good, the upper ends would only be reached periodically in the rainy season) if you do respiratory illness will quickly follow. your little dragon wont stay small for long and the Australian frilled dragons can exceed 90cm in length (larger than he PNG ones) they are voracious, also in the wild I've always found they prefer vertical trees and stumps, so give him some of those, they like to shimmy around them to get out of sight
